## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics rate law identification. The relationship typically follows power-law, rational, or exponential forms depending on the reaction mechanism.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with equilibrium back-reaction)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or surface reaction saturation)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic growth/consumption)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate law with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding kinetics)
- Second-order reversible: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law from reversible bimolecular reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence with no explicit time → autonomous ODE rate law, likely simple reaction order mechanism
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic mechanism where product catalyzes reaction
- Rate that saturates at high concentration → surface-limited or enzyme-limited process, use rational functions A/(K+A)
- Negative rate values (consumption) with magnitude increasing with A → simple forward reaction with positive order
- Rate law with both positive and negative terms in A → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Integer vs fractional reaction orders → elementary vs complex/apparent mechanism distinction
- Rate depending on both A and t explicitly → non-isothermal conditions, photolysis, or catalyst deactivation
- Quadratic dependence on A → bimolecular step as rate-determining step in mechanism
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches a nonzero constant → equilibrium concentration, model as c0*(A - A_eq) terms
